<div id="review_1968696447" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1968696447" />
    <a title="Sandi (Zorena)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4861650-sandi-zorena"><img alt="Sandi (Zorena)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1380040078p2/4861650.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1968696447?book_show_action=true">Mar 30, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sandi (Zorena)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sandi (Zorena)" href="/user/show/4861650-sandi-zorena">Sandi (Zorena)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780151012381" href="/book/show/2525.Seeing">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4861650-sandi-zorena?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4861650-sandi-zorena?shelf=science-fiction-dystopian">science-fiction-dystopian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1968696447" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17842227460218150412">I found this book far less visceral than Blindness which made me enjoy it a lot more. Whereas the first book showed how base humans become when left to their own with no policing Seeing shows how base a government becomes.<br/><br/>Set anywhere in Portugal and at anytime in the modern world this somewhat dystopian tale tells us how a government deals with an unusual mass occurrence. It's voting day and close to 80% of the population of the capitol city have decided to turn in blank ballots. <br/><br/>At first thing</span>
  <span id="freeText17842227460218150412" style="display:none">I found this book far less visceral than Blindness which made me enjoy it a lot more. Whereas the first book showed how base humans become when left to their own with no policing Seeing shows how base a government becomes.<br /><br />Set anywhere in Portugal and at anytime in the modern world this somewhat dystopian tale tells us how a government deals with an unusual mass occurrence. It's voting day and close to 80% of the population of the capitol city have decided to turn in blank ballots. <br /><br />At first things are humorous but soon events take a darker turn but only on the side of the government. The populous carries on normally as if nothing untoward has happened. <br /><br />Saramago shows his mastery of the intricacies of a government so determined to be right that it goes to any length to prove it. He does it all with a simple telling of sometimes mundane conversations and occurances. There's no false suspense here. <br /><br />Personally I love his style but I do warn you that it's not for everyone. It's a flow of consciousness with very little proper grammar but that's what makes this story work for me. If you liked Blindness I highly suggest this book as the better of the two.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17842227460218150412" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1897213719" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1897213719" />
    <a title="Marc" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2876105-marc"><img alt="Marc" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1569160429p2/2876105.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1897213719?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marc" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marc" href="/user/show/2876105-marc">Marc</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9789029075695" href="/book/show/6891256-de-stad-der-zienden">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2876105-marc?shelf=portugese-literature">portugese-literature</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1897213719" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13456805642618481488">It is the wet dream of every anarchist: a society without government, without coercion and repression, where everything runs by itself, where everyone knows his place and does his duty. In this book Saramago outlines such a situation in an unnamed capital. The city is completely abandoned by the government, in a panic reaction because in two successive elections the citizens had voted blank. The focus is not so much on the anarchist virtues, but on the cramped and especially cynical way in which</span>
  <span id="freeText13456805642618481488" style="display:none">It is the wet dream of every anarchist: a society without government, without coercion and repression, where everything runs by itself, where everyone knows his place and does his duty. In this book Saramago outlines such a situation in an unnamed capital. The city is completely abandoned by the government, in a panic reaction because in two successive elections the citizens had voted blank. The focus is not so much on the anarchist virtues, but on the cramped and especially cynical way in which the politicians and government leaders respond to this tacit popular uprising. <br /><br />Saramago here unleashes his most fierce sarcastic talents, resulting in hilarious conversations between ministers of government, in which the world is turned upside down, showing how gruesome the exercise of power can be. Simply delicious! <br /><br />But after about 200 pages the author suddenly changes tack and turns the story into a sequel to his masterly novel "City of Blindness". Out of the blue a number of characters from that novel emerge again. It is not entirely clear to me what the point of this is, and what it adds to the story. In addition, Saramago gets lost in side intrigues about a at first stern, but then very conscentious police officer. No, this "Seeing" – apart from the absurd sarcasm in the first half of the novel – does not reach the level of the fabulous "Blindness".</span>
  <a data-text-id="13456805642618481488" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6445448254417276722">Reading Saramago is a lot like reading Faulkner. Once you get into his sentence structure and lack of punctuation, it's an entertaining read and you feel smarter when you're done. Like all the book reviewers say on the cover, this is a fascinating look not only at the people in government but also at how they react to crisis. As with Blindness, the book that precedes Seeing, this book left me asking, "so what happened?" or "how did it end?" Guess that's up to me, but I hope there's a third book </span>
  <span id="freeText6445448254417276722" style="display:none">Reading Saramago is a lot like reading Faulkner. Once you get into his sentence structure and lack of punctuation, it's an entertaining read and you feel smarter when you're done. Like all the book reviewers say on the cover, this is a fascinating look not only at the people in government but also at how they react to crisis. As with Blindness, the book that precedes Seeing, this book left me asking, "so what happened?" or "how did it end?" Guess that's up to me, but I hope there's a third book in this series that answers a few questions!<br /><br />The excerpts below are two of my favorite lines of prose (not spoilers) and they may well explain why Seeing won't be the last of Saramago's novels that I read.<br /><br />"We are born, and at that moment, it is as if we had signed a pact for the rest of our life, but a day may come when we will ask ourselves Who signed this on my behalf."<br /><br />"Perfect moments, especially when they verge on the sublime, have the grave disadvantage of being very short-lived, which fact, being obvious, we would not need to mention were it not that they have a still greater disadvantage, which is that we do not know what do once they are over."</span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1132127925" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1132127925" />
    <a title="David" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8311987-david"><img alt="David" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411759189p2/8311987.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1132127925?book_show_action=true">Dec 14, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David" href="/user/show/8311987-david">David</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1132127925" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer585923392864009736">Like Blindness, Seeing is an exploration of a 'what if' scenario. For an unstated reason, 83% of the population casts blank votes in national elections, and continues to do so in subsequent 'runoff' elections. This causes a flurry of activity by the government (hinted to be the author's home country, Portugal) which becomes increasing nefarious and dark. The capital is put under siege by its own government, and when this fails to warrant a response from the docile populace, the government evacua</span>
  <span id="freeText585923392864009736" style="display:none">Like Blindness, Seeing is an exploration of a 'what if' scenario. For an unstated reason, 83% of the population casts blank votes in national elections, and continues to do so in subsequent 'runoff' elections. This causes a flurry of activity by the government (hinted to be the author's home country, Portugal) which becomes increasing nefarious and dark. The capital is put under siege by its own government, and when this fails to warrant a response from the docile populace, the government evacuates in a hope to further isolate and cause the people to 'come to their senses.'<br /><br />Needless to say, this does not happen; and this is where the book takes a turn for the Machiavellian; the government takes increasingly hostile actions against the capital, cordoning it off from the rest of the nation, manipulating the press, committing treasonous actions against their own citizens, engages in rampant surveillance, and ultimately finding scapegoats in a small group of people who survived the blindness epidemic of the first book.<br /><br />We are introduced to the main character, the Superintendent, approximately halfway through the book, although his archetype was present in inchoate stages throughout the novel. He is a just man, and is willing to adhere to his principles, and indeed, do what is right in a world where the interests of the state have become the supreme arbiter of truth, lies, right, wrong, life, death, information, and justice. The book asks so many questions about the nature of democracy, how it is corrupted, and the question of 'choice,' not only in terms of if it exists when choosing political affiliation, but in the face of humanity's failings, such as lust for power, control, corruption, and complicity.<br /><br />I won't say this is Saramago's best work, as he is one of the most brilliant authors I have as yet come across, but it is a powerful and immensely disturbing one, even if it does meander and fall down rabbit holes of digression from time to time. It is at times satirical, powerful, damning of the human condition, humorous, disturbing, and as always, the prose is exquisite.</span>
  <a data-text-id="585923392864009736" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_356635639" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/356635639" />
    <a title="Nigeyb" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10301421-nigeyb"><img alt="Nigeyb" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593065725p2/10301421.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/356635639?book_show_action=true">Jun 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nigeyb" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nigeyb" href="/user/show/10301421-nigeyb">Nigeyb</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer356635639" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1338066496024014373">I read this book shortly after having completed 'Blindness'. 'Seeing' is a sequel to 'Blindness'. <br/><br/>At first there appears to be little to explicitly link the two books. This book's premise is a subconscious revolution whereby the inhabitants of a city start to behave in a curiously collective manner - 83% of them cast a blank ballot at a general election. This inevitably creates confusion and panic within the government. <br/><br/>Like 'Blindness', part of my pleasure in this book was due to Saramago's unu</span>
  <span id="freeText1338066496024014373" style="display:none">I read this book shortly after having completed 'Blindness'. 'Seeing' is a sequel to 'Blindness'. <br /><br />At first there appears to be little to explicitly link the two books. This book's premise is a subconscious revolution whereby the inhabitants of a city start to behave in a curiously collective manner - 83% of them cast a blank ballot at a general election. This inevitably creates confusion and panic within the government. <br /><br />Like 'Blindness', part of my pleasure in this book was due to Saramago's unusual and distinctive narrative style. Again, there are no quotation marks for dialogue, and many long sentences which frequently have a "stream of consciousness" quality. Characters are never identified by their proper names. Despite this the book is easy to follow. <br /><br />It took me about 100 pages to really get into this book. It's at around the 100 page mark that the book shifts from being focussed on the government's reaction to the blank votes, to a story involving the main characters from 'Blindness' and some undercover policemen. The book became more absorbing and compelling from this moment. <br /><br />Saramago poses profound questions whilst providing plenty of his deadpan, wry humour mainly at the expense of hierarchy and bureaucracy. The book holds up a mirror to the modern democratic process; the farcical nature of hierarchy; political "spin"; and the corruption that inevitably accompanies power. The book becomes more unsettling and disturbing as it reaches its conclusion. That said, there is also a positive message around personal choice and redemption. By the end there is much to ponder, and I think the book would make an excellent choice for a book group to discuss. This is a challenging and original political and sociological satire. Well worth reading.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1338066496024014373" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_192174732" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/192174732" />
    <a title="Larry Bassett" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3816725-larry-bassett"><img alt="Larry Bassett" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1390874855p2/3816725.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/192174732?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Larry Bassett" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Larry Bassett" href="/user/show/3816725-larry-bassett">Larry Bassett</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780151012381" href="/book/show/2525.Seeing">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3816725-larry-bassett?shelf=political">political</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3816725-larry-bassett?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer192174732" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12678446616687135742">The author of <i>Seeing</i>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1285555.Jos__Saramago' title='José Saramago' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jose Saramago</a>, won the Nobel Prize in Literature in 1998. He said at the Nobel Prize Banquet: <br/><br/><blockquote> In this half-century, obviously governments have not morally done for human rights all that they should. The injustices multiply, the inequalities get worse, the ignorance grows, the misery expands. This same schizophrenic humanity that has the capacity to send instruments to a planet to study the composition of its rocks can with indifference note the deaths of millions of people</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText12678446616687135742" style="display:none">The author of <i>Seeing</i>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1285555.Jos__Saramago" title="José Saramago" rel="nofollow noopener">Jose Saramago</a>, won the Nobel Prize in Literature in 1998. He said at the Nobel Prize Banquet: <br /><br /><blockquote> In this half-century, obviously governments have not morally done for human rights all that they should. The injustices multiply, the inequalities get worse, the ignorance grows, the misery expands. This same schizophrenic humanity that has the capacity to send instruments to a planet to study the composition of its rocks can with indifference note the deaths of millions of people from starvation. To go to Mars seems more easy than going to the neighbour. Nobody performs her or his duties. Governments do not, because they do not know, they are not able or they do not wish, or because they are not permitted by those who effectively govern the world: The multinational and pluricontinental companies whose power - absolutely non-democratic - reduce to next to nothing what is left of the ideal of democracy. </blockquote><br /><br />His obituary in June, 2010 in the NY Times noted that “He described globalization as the new totalitarianism and lamented contemporary democracy’s failure to stem the increasing powers of multinational corporations.”<br /><br />His views on government are a part of the satire and irony and paradox and ridicule that is evident in <i>Seeing</i>. The book would do well in a graphic presentation due to its comedic words and actions. <br /><br />The NY Times review of <i>Seeing</i> is delightful both in its synopsis and its analysis.<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.nytimes.com/2006/04/09/books/review/09rafferty.html">http://www.nytimes.com/2006/04/09/boo...</a><br />It is also not totally impressed with the work which also makes it more interesting to read.<br /><br /><i>Seeing</i> has been translated into English from its original Portuguese. The lack of much punctuation has also been translated. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2526.Blindness" title="Blindness by José Saramago" rel="nofollow noopener">Blindness</a> is a similar “what if?” book that immediately precedes it.<br /> <br />The book is two books in writing style: the first half with minimal formatting and Saramago’s traditionally long sentences. There are more periods (but still no quotation marks) in the back half and it settles into a quasi detective format. This happened just in time for me as the satire was getting a bit repetitious. Big, bad government throughout. And since we are outside looking in, we can easily see how outrageous it is – and yet it seems like it could almost be real. Wink, wink! Given the choice, the companion books should be read in chronological order: <i>Blindness</i> then <i>Seeing</i>. This is not mandatory, however.<br /><br />The book was fun to read though perhaps ultimately a little heavy-handed with the humor, especially during the opening half. OK Jose, I get it! But no humor at the end. Dead serious. For political satire with a message, this is as good as it gets: four stars and a recommendation to check it out. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12678446616687135742" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_16357393" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/16357393" />
    <a title="Brian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18549-brian"><img alt="Brian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1512310401p2/18549.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/16357393?book_show_action=true">Feb 25, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brian" href="/user/show/18549-brian">Brian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer16357393" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1044706696453792634">Resurrecting themes initially explored in his epic "Blindness" (which I highly, highly recommend), Saramago's unusual sequel starts of with just as much bang: Election day in an unnamed city in an unnnamed country, and the polls are empty. All of a sudden, directly following an intense rainstorm, everyone in the city arrives to cast their votes at once. Upon counting these votes it is discovered that 7 out of 10 are blank. A vote is recast, spies are integrated into the general populace to deter</span>
  <span id="freeText1044706696453792634" style="display:none">Resurrecting themes initially explored in his epic "Blindness" (which I highly, highly recommend), Saramago's unusual sequel starts of with just as much bang: Election day in an unnamed city in an unnnamed country, and the polls are empty. All of a sudden, directly following an intense rainstorm, everyone in the city arrives to cast their votes at once. Upon counting these votes it is discovered that 7 out of 10 are blank. A vote is recast, spies are integrated into the general populace to determine what and if there is conspiracy among this nation's citizens, but no concrete evidence presents itself. After counting the votes at the end of the second attempt, 9 out of 10 are blank. The government declares a state of panic, and then proceeds to manufacure such a catastrophe among its people. <br /><br />It's an intense story, certainly, entirely a pro pos of today's current events. "Seeing" draws many of Saramago's literary fortes: a non-specific and widespread malaise affecting an entire nation, bureaucratic impotence in the face of disaster, and the shocking after-effects of a collective mob mentality. I found this particular translation (from portuguese) poetic and moving. Recommended. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1044706696453792634" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1799009019" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1799009019" />
    <a title="Lily S. " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22201823-lily-s"><img alt="Lily S. " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452469573p2/22201823.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1799009019?book_show_action=true">Nov 28, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lily S. " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lily S. " href="/user/show/22201823-lily-s">Lily S. </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone living in a totalitarian state </span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1799009019" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12280687709608949886">One of the best reads I had this year without a doubt. <br/><br/>More than 300 pages of walls of text, textbook style except worse punctuation. <br/><br/>One day people decide to hand in empty white sheets on the general elections. The government moves from town and tries to bring back the old order of things with different methods and in the emerging crisis of the democratic system a few people face some serious moral decisions. <br/><br/>This is the story told in a paragraph without spoiling anything but there are truly so</span>
  <span id="freeText12280687709608949886" style="display:none">One of the best reads I had this year without a doubt. <br /><br />More than 300 pages of walls of text, textbook style except worse punctuation. <br /><br />One day people decide to hand in empty white sheets on the general elections. The government moves from town and tries to bring back the old order of things with different methods and in the emerging crisis of the democratic system a few people face some serious moral decisions. <br /><br />This is the story told in a paragraph without spoiling anything but there are truly so many layers that one could wrote hundreds of pages about them. <br /><br />It's an interesting study of freedom and revolution, which makes it very actual since totalitarian leaders are on the rise all over Europe and the states are moving away from liberalism as well. <br /><br />It's good to keep in mind that real revolutions has to be based on mutual aid and compassion instead of using the same tactics that the ones in power use to control people and maintain their power. And that one can be free even when there are walls built around them. This book is a very powerful reminder that it's the people who actually have the power. <br /><br />It's a great sequel, highly connected to the first part because only after Blindness can Seeing come. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12280687709608949886" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/6088060?book_show_action=true">Sep 12, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lori" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lori" href="/user/show/369169-lori">Lori</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer6088060" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4472366229255668657">As the "Somewhat" sequel to Blindness, this book follows the same townspeople, 4 years later, around election time. Believed to be under the "spell" of the one woman who did not go blind during the afflicted period 4 years earlier, the voters come out late, as if instructed to do so,and a shocking 80% have posted blank ballots. <br/><br/>The goverment once again reacts atrociously, and places the townspeople under lockdown, and begins an investigation. However, where this book varies from the first... we </span>
  <span id="freeText4472366229255668657" style="display:none">As the "Somewhat" sequel to Blindness, this book follows the same townspeople, 4 years later, around election time. Believed to be under the "spell" of the one woman who did not go blind during the afflicted period 4 years earlier, the voters come out late, as if instructed to do so,and a shocking 80% have posted blank ballots. <br /><br />The goverment once again reacts atrociously, and places the townspeople under lockdown, and begins an investigation. However, where this book varies from the first... we see the townspeople reaching out to one another and helping one another, and coming together in this time of adversary.<br /><br />If you enjoyed Blindness, you should defintely pick this one up. If you are thinking of reading this one 1st, I would suggest reading Blindness first, as it will lead you to a better understanding of the novel and its predictament.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ocN4IkL+4SEaxTMs/PEgqQYIMaMxWgxtMUyODG3dJnvc6+J7T6z3XSYBY1EUhOScjSrC4TQAplu2+e+hBKBW8A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('2pR4SpY5aZHN9Ky6c+ec8Te6vCLtxxaSuBilgfIR6N2nvOITm2t/7fEw/MebkljEvJhPYOidvKQ/rcQsm2yYVg==')})
  }

//<![CDATA[
      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_11502462'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11502462?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">بیشعوری، راهنمای تشخیص و درمان خطرناکترین بیماری تاریخ بشریت<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/56272.Xavier_Crement?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Xavier Crement<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p6\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p0\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p0\"><\/span><\/span> 2.91 avg rating &mdash; 3,641 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 1990\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer16504644090414075923\">خاویر کرمنت نویسنده کتاب بیشعوری 26 سال پیش نسبت به شخصیت دونالد ترامپ هشدار می‌دهد و به طور آشکار او را بیشعور می‌خواند. در جایی از کتاب بیشعوری به کتاب مقدس بیشعورهای تاجر به نام «هنر دزدی» اثر «دونالد کرامپ» اشاره می‌شود. که مقصود نویسنده کتاب «هن<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText16504644090414075923\" style=\"display:none\">خاویر کرمنت نویسنده کتاب بیشعوری 26 سال پیش نسبت به شخصیت دونالد ترامپ هشدار می‌دهد و به طور آشکار او را بیشعور می‌خواند. در جایی از کتاب بیشعوری به کتاب مقدس بیشعورهای تاجر به نام «هنر دزدی» اثر «دونالد کرامپ» اشاره می‌شود. که مقصود نویسنده کتاب «هنر معامله» نوشته «دونالد ترامپ»، رئیس جمهور فعلی آمریکا، است.\nدر کتاب می شنویم:\n«کتاب مقدس این نوع بیشعورها (بیشعورهای تاجر) کتابی است به نام هنر دزدی از دونالد کرامپ که می‌نویسد:«راستی و درستی، مهمل و بی‌معنی اند. همیشه مفیدترین راهکارها در تجارت، مدیریت درستکاری عداد و ارقام است. چرا باید برای به‌دست آوردن چیزی به سختی و با صداقت کار کرد وقتی می‌توان آن را به راحتی دزدید؟»\nچاره‌ای هم نیست وقتی یک نفر با کمبود لیاقت و توانایی اصرار داشته باشد که در جلسات، مذاکرات و محاسبات به هر نحوی کارش را پیش ببرد، باید کمبودهایش را با حقه بازی، حرافی و بلوف زدن جبران کند. بیشعورهای گنده‌گو از همینجا پیدا می‌شوند. او هنرنمایی یک گنده‌گو وقتی است که سرنخ کلام از دستش رفته باشد و نداند درباره چی حرف می‌زند. چنین بیشعوری خودش را در برانگیختن دیگران (چرندگویی)، خلاقیت(دزدیدن ایده‌های دیگران)، تعامل (ارعاب دیگران) و مدیریت (سرپوش گذاشتن بر گندکاری‌هایش) خبره نشان می‌دهد.\nکتاب صوتی بیشعوری اثر خاویر کرمنت است. نویسنده ای که بیست سال آزگار با بیشعوری خود، خانواده و اطرافیانش را آزار داد. از دید او تقریبا همه افراد بیشعورند. اگر معتقدید که بهتر است کرمنت درمورد زندگی خودش نظر بدهد باید بگویم بی شعوری یک بیماری است که اغلب افراد مبتلا، از آن بی اطلاع هستند و معمولا در قبال این اتهام می گویند: من بي‌شعور نيستم، تو بیشعوري. بعضي خصوصيات مشترك بیشعورها از اين قرار است: خودپسندي فجيع، نفرت انگيزي بي حد، خيرخواهي متكبرانه، ضميرناخودآگاه غيرقابل نفوذ، كسب قدرت با خوار و ضعيف كردن ديگران، امتنا از صفات اصلي انساني و سوءاستفاده بي رحمانه از آدم های ساده. اگر هنوز هم فکر می کنید که تنها همسایه بی ملاحظه یا مدیر بی احساستان گرفتار بیشعوری هستند پیشنهاد می کنم این کتاب را گوش کنید تا با مثال های ملموس خاویر کرمنت مصداق های بارز بیشعوری را در خود و اطرافتان ببینید.\n\nاین کتاب در سال 1990 در امریکا منتشر شد و محمود فرجامی آن را اولین بار در سال 1390 به زبان فارسی ترجمه نمود. هرچند به دلیل نگرفتن مجوز چاپ آن را به صورت اینترنتی منتشر کرد تا بالاخره در سال 1394 به صورت چاپی در ویترین کتاب فروشی ها قرار گرفت. این کتاب در ایران از همان ابتدا با استقبال فراوانی مواجه شد که البته نثر روان و طنزآلود فرجامی در این محبوبیت بی تأثیر نبوده است.\n\nبیشعوری نوعی اعتیاد است مثل اعتیاد به مواد مخدر یا الکل. فرد معتاد تمایل به تکرار کار خود دارد و این اعتیاد از فرد به جامعه سرایت می کند و محیطی آزاردهنده را به وجود می آورد. بیشعورها چندین دسته اند و ویژگی های مشخصی دارند. آن ها قانون های نانوشته ای دارند، مثلا: تمام قوانين براي اين به وجود آمده‌اند كه نقض شوند، اما فقط تو، حق داري كه آن را زيرپا بگذاري نه ديگران و یا تمام مشكلات را ديگران به وجود آورده‌اند. آن ها بر این باورند که علت اعتراض مهم نيست. مهم خود اعتراض كردن است كه به خاطر آن زندگي مي کنند و همواره معترضند.\n\nکمترین بهره ای که پس از شنیدن کتاب می برید، این است که می توانید بیشعورها را بشناسید و از آن ها دوری کنید اما، شاید آنچه که در این کتاب صوتی شنونده را بیش از یک کتاب طنز و یا بیانگر واقعیت های تلخ اجتماعی با خود همراه می کند نشان دادن روش برخورد با بیشعورها و چگونگی درمان بیشعوری است. خاویر کرمنت انواع و اقسام مثال ها از انسان های بیشعور را با ذکر جزئی ترین رفتارها بیان می کند و چون این فضا قصه های واقعی از زندگی خود و نزدیکانش را به همراه دارد شیرینی دوچندانی به کتاب می بخشد.\n\nهرکسی گفته هیچ بیشعوری در دنیا وجود ندارد، خودش هم بیشعور است. من سه تا بچه بیشعور دارم و هر روز دارم هر چهارتاشان را تحمل می کنم. آخر شوهرم هم بیشعور است.\n- خاویر کرمنت؛           <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/1285555.Jos_Saramago"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1497455560p3/1285555.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/1285555.Jos_Saramago">José Saramago
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
12,208
followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4070604988240625601">José Saramago is one of the most important international writers of the last hundred years. Born in Portugal in 1922, he was in his sixties when he came to prominence as a writer with the publication of Baltasar and Blimunda. A huge body of work followed, translated into more than forty languages, and in 1998 he was awarded the Nobel Prize in Literature. Saramago died in June 2010.</span>

</div>
